<div id="review_3075250635" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3075250635" />
    <a title="Diana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28386638-diana"><img alt="Diana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431331494p2/28386638.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3075250635?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diana" href="/user/show/28386638-diana">Diana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/41818297-where-the-forest-meets-the-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386638-diana?shelf=maybe-i-m-being-an-asshole-but">maybe-i-m-being-an-asshole-but</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3075250635" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17981856637408597769">I grabbed this as an kindle first read, and I'm sorry to say that it was kind of trash. Worse yet, it didn't start out trash, so I unfortunately wasted a lot more time than I would have trying to speed read the end. I have no idea what book everyone else is reviewing with their five stars, and I'm mad about that, too. Y'all need higher standards, and you can fight me on that, if you like. ¯\_(ツ)_/¯<br/><br/>The premise is pretty great, and the execution to begin with is alright if not luminous; we have a </span>
  <span id="freeText17981856637408597769" style="display:none">I grabbed this as an kindle first read, and I'm sorry to say that it was kind of trash. Worse yet, it didn't start out trash, so I unfortunately wasted a lot more time than I would have trying to speed read the end. I have no idea what book everyone else is reviewing with their five stars, and I'm mad about that, too. Y'all need higher standards, and you can fight me on that, if you like. ¯\_(ツ)_/¯<br /><br />The premise is pretty great, and the execution to begin with is alright if not luminous; we have a grad student who's had it totally rough trying to sort out her shit, waylaid by a little girl that she's trying her best to help, and their interaction is interesting. I didn't like Jo from the start, though, mainly because of her total lack of give a shit for the stray dog that the girl befriends. At some point in time later in the book, her advisor's like, "oh jo, you have such a big heart", and I'm like, oh yeah no-- ask the dog about that. TW:<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The dog gets shot in the end though, so here's another big ol' fuck off for that. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />We the meet the Egg Man, Gabe, who's a depressed hottie backwoods farmer, but a brainiac in disguise; Tabby, Jo's BFF who is an extreme manic pixie girl, and various other characters that are either extremely likable or extremely unlikeable; there is no in-between. The dialog was wobbly all the way through, and the treatment of Gabe's mental illness is a goddamn mess. Not gonna lie, I should have put it down when Jo dismissed it and he was like , YOU ARE CORRECT, ALL I NEEDED WAS TO GET OUT OF BED AND GET SOME FRESH AIR. THUMBS UP AND THANKS, FRIENDOS!" But, damnably, I was holding out for Ursa's real story, and once the ending happened, I was sorry I did.<br /><br />I'm not sure the author did any research on the subject of mental illness, or if she did, it happened via internet, and there's an essential oils huckster out there that convinced her that all you need to feel better is to acknowledge your issue and just get out there while smelling of bergamot, sport. Gabe goes from having depression, anxiety and agoraphobia to just being like cool cool, full hospital in a city I can't stand? no problem, I can sit here in the lobby with my NEW GIRLFRIEND. NBD. And drugs? Nah, he doesn't need those, because he doesn't need those chemicals in his head. (cue juggernaut gif here); his sister Lacey goes from turbo bitch who's hated and resented him all her life *and tried to lose him in the woods once* to super cool older sister who admits her mistakes and thinks of him fondly because Gabe made the family talk about The Big Secret once. ONCE. And Ursa, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ who as it turns out is just a kid that escaped attempted sexual violence and murder at the hands of a couple of crackheads that killed her mother and dissassociated, gets shoved into telling the truth thanks to the fear of never seeing Jo or Gabe again, and then is like, nah, I'm a genius intellect and therefore I can mind-over-matter this shit over the course of just a few months.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />My eyes just rolled so far up I rediscovered a childhood memory. Please. If you are a writer, do not do this shit. This is literally akin to writing a story about a paraplegic who refuses drugs because Reasons, then is suddenly able to walk after being positively encouraged by someone they would like to bone or by whom they would like to be mothered. <br /><br />Ugh, ok. But finally, as I mentioned earlier, while the story started out ok, it just went downhill from there. Gabe has no discernible personality other than Troubled Hot Man That Jo Can Fix Lickety Split, and the dialog is choppy-wobbles all the time, but by the time we get to the last 20% of the book, omg. it's bad, guys. Suddenly a cast of social workers and cops are introduced, everyone gets a personality implant, there's a training montage in hospital, Tabby is shown to be a saintly manic pixie girl, and an entire, unbelievable, cheesy-ass hallmark movie is crammed in.<br /><br />Guys, do you remember in The Eyre Affair when the detectives are able to defeat a villain by using unlabeled dialog? hilarious, I know, even though a good author with strong character voices can get away with swatches of unlabeled dialog just fine. Vanderah? Cannot get away with this. In the last section of the book, there were consistent conversations between Jo and Gabe where I had no idea who was talking because they just bled into one another so desperately. It was painful. Of course, that lack of direction and cohesiveness bleeds all through the end of this story such that no part of it is pleasant after a certain point. I don't know; my review is suddenly suffering the same problem because I've lost the will to give a shit about it myself, and that should also count for something.<br /><br />Honestly, people. Standards.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17981856637408597769" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2785362746" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2785362746" />
    <a title="Susan&#39;s Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19736308-susan-s-reviews"><img alt="Susan&#39;s Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507651790p2/19736308.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2785362746?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan&#39;s Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan&#39;s Reviews" href="/user/show/19736308-susan-s-reviews">Susan&#39;s Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/41818297-where-the-forest-meets-the-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2785362746" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6352950990717081735">Where the Forest Meets the Stars is definitely quirky - something I always enjoy in a novel when it is done right, and Ursa pulled off the quirky element perfectly! Is Ursa really an extra-terrestrial? Right up until the very end, you will be left wondering! This novel deals with child abuse, breast cancer and PTSD. Despite these heavy themes, the story is still hopeful and up-beat. All three of the main characters manage to survive their particular "hell on earth".<br/><br/>Three very damaged people (Jo,</span>
  <span id="freeText6352950990717081735" style="display:none">Where the Forest Meets the Stars is definitely quirky - something I always enjoy in a novel when it is done right, and Ursa pulled off the quirky element perfectly! Is Ursa really an extra-terrestrial? Right up until the very end, you will be left wondering! This novel deals with child abuse, breast cancer and PTSD. Despite these heavy themes, the story is still hopeful and up-beat. All three of the main characters manage to survive their particular "hell on earth".<br /><br />Three very damaged people (Jo, Gabe and Ursa) come together to form their own little family and support group. Of course, Child Services and the legal authorities can't see their odd relationship in the same positive way.<br /><br />This was an unconventional love story, where hope and love and "five miracles" triumphed over the terrible traumas which had affected Jo, Gabe and the indomitable Ursa. Hard to believe that this was the author's debut novel - well done!<br />Highly recommended!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6352950990717081735" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2751140229" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2751140229" />
    <a title="Mel (Epic Reading)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7074816-mel-epic-reading"><img alt="Mel (Epic Reading)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487568293p2/7074816.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2751140229?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mel (Epic Reading)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mel (Epic Reading)" href="/user/show/7074816-mel-epic-reading">Mel (Epic Reading)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7074816-mel-epic-reading?shelf=library-print">library-print</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7074816-mel-epic-reading?shelf=arc-netgalley">arc-netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2751140229" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18313005797768667296">The beauty of this book is that you want to believe Ursa’s alien story; and at times start to think maybe it is true. Glendy Vanderah gives our little girl, Ursa, such a strong, passionate and intelligent voice that it’s impossible not to fall in love with her. As I thought might happen by the end of the novel I was bawling my eyes out. For so many reasons and at so many levels; none of which felt cheap or convenient. <br/><br/><b>Characters</b><br/>Each character we encounter is unique and each has their own challen</span>
  <span id="freeText18313005797768667296" style="display:none">The beauty of this book is that you want to believe Ursa’s alien story; and at times start to think maybe it is true. Glendy Vanderah gives our little girl, Ursa, such a strong, passionate and intelligent voice that it’s impossible not to fall in love with her. As I thought might happen by the end of the novel I was bawling my eyes out. For so many reasons and at so many levels; none of which felt cheap or convenient. <br /><br /><b>Characters</b><br />Each character we encounter is unique and each has their own challenges. Individually these people felt like real people; who all have complex issues. From Gabe, a reclusive depressive 20 something who can’t get away as he cares for his ailing mother; to Jo, our strong lead female who has undergone a full mastectomy (before she reached 25 years of age), a recent orphan and full-time PhD student; to Tabby who is the kind of bubbly crazy friend that always knows how to do something seemingly insane to get a smile. Even out periphery characters are given enough life to feel like I could relate them back to real people I know. <br /><br /><b>Plot </b><br />This is a character drive story at its core. While the plot is very interesting (and gives us some tense and terrifying moments); the reality is that it’s less about a little girl who just shows up one day with no parents (and no one reporting her missing), and more about the love that grows between the child, our lead Jo and Jo’s possible love interest Gabe. Each of them struggles with their current life and each of them transforms through the book. <br /><br /><b>Miracles </b><br />I love how adorable Ursa’s ‘miracles’ are. I won’t spoil them for you; but it’s so heart warming and an important reminder that what may seem a miracle to one feels commonplace to another. And that we all experience miracles on a semi-regular basis; we’ve just lost the ability to see them as the miracles they are. This is a perfect book for someone who might be struggling to overcome a tough time or incident in their life. As all three characters are also doing so; but more importantly the reminder that miracles happen everyday; you just have to look for them. <br /><br /><b>Overall </b><br />Right from the opening line I was intrigued and ready to jump into this story. How can you not be curious when the first sentence is:<br /><i>”The girl could be a changeling.”</i><br />It reminded me of the straightforward, to the point opening lines of Dickens. “The Marleys were dead to begin with”; the line is both enchanting, setting a mood and letting you know right away that something might be a bit off in this novel you’re about to encounter. <br />A couple months ago I thought Miracle Creek would be the best debut novel of 2019. Where the Forest meets the Stars has blown Miracle Creek out of the water and solidly affirmed itself as one of the best debut novels I have ever read (never mind for just 2019). I hope to see a lot more from Vanderah. Although I wouldn’t mind if the next story was a little less teary near the end (it’s just so embarrassing to tear-up on the bus). <br /><br /><i>Please note: I received an eARC of this book from the publisher via NetGalley. This is an honest and unbiased review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="18313005797768667296" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2702391516" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2702391516" />
    <a title="Mehvish Z Zaidi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7280200-mehvish-z-zaidi"><img alt="Mehvish Z Zaidi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564365800p2/7280200.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2702391516?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mehvish Z Zaidi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mehvish Z Zaidi" href="/user/show/7280200-mehvish-z-zaidi">Mehvish Z Zaidi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2702391516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6219198066249849974">Where the Forest Meets the Stars was my bookclub’s March pick. Mostly, I do not like to dive into a book blind and usually do my homework before I start it. I read the blurb and check out the Goodreads ratings, look at the percentage of the stars given, sometimes I skim through the reviews if the ratings are mixed. On Goodreads, this book had an average rating of 4.24, with 82% of the 16,185 readers had given it either 4 or 5 stars. Now, that is something. My fellow bookclub readers, the ones wh</span>
  <span id="freeText6219198066249849974" style="display:none">Where the Forest Meets the Stars was my bookclub’s March pick. Mostly, I do not like to dive into a book blind and usually do my homework before I start it. I read the blurb and check out the Goodreads ratings, look at the percentage of the stars given, sometimes I skim through the reviews if the ratings are mixed. On Goodreads, this book had an average rating of 4.24, with 82% of the 16,185 readers had given it either 4 or 5 stars. Now, that is something. My fellow bookclub readers, the ones who had finished earlier, raved about it; claiming each word had to be savoured. Needless to say, my excitement to read was sky-high and expectations from this book were tremendous. However, unfortunately, this book failed to create an impression on me like it did on the rest of the readers.<br /><br />The story, in my humble opinion, is not unique or extraordinary. The novel revolves around three central characters. First is an eight year old girl named Ursa who claims she is an alien looking for five miracles on Earth and after finding them she will return to her home planet. Second; Jo, a cancer survivor and an ornithologist who is dealing with loss of her parent and third; Gabe, a young man who battles with mental illness and is looking after his mother. The lives of these three characters entwine as the story develops and they deal with their respective issues individually and collectively. <br /><br />I reckon the writing did not work for me, I found it to be inconsistent and inexpert. <br /><br />“But who was reflected there, the old Jo or the new almost Jo?”<br /><br />The pace was sluggish until the last twenty-five percent or so of the book. The story felt routined and fragmented in the first quarter of the book. I really liked Ursa’s character. Her intelligence and curiosity was well described by Glendy Vanderah. She was intriguing and interesting and had enough mystery surrounding her that I wanted to continue reading just to find out more about her. On the other hand, I could not like Jo’s character at all. I wanted to sympathise with her because of all that she had suffered but I just could not do it. I found her attitude towards Gabe’s depression to be selfish and insensitive. The scene where she almost forced him to shave off his beard, knowing why he kept it and the significance of it, made me furious. It was not her decision to make and her reasoning behind it — <br /><br />“Don’t you want to be irresistible to me?” <br /><br />Her attitude towards his depression and agoraphobia was deplorable, like he could snap out of it and was just making excuses not to do so. <br /><br />“This is my world, Gabe. If you could find a way to be in it, everything would be much simpler.” <br /><br />In my opinion, the author has taken a very casual attitude towards depression and agoraphobia and did not treat them with the attention and seriousness that they deserve. Depression and agoraphobia are challenging diseases that people suffer from despite have a strong and loving support system. A lack of support system may make dealing with the illness more difficult but a new romantic attachment, like Gabe and Jo’s in the story, does not miraculously make the symptoms disappear. <br /><br />I liked the idea of connection of lost souls and fighting for a family that one may make for oneself but Where the Forest Meets the Stars lacked the finesse in execution of that idea. This book did not work for me however, if you’re a fan of feel-good light fiction and are willing to stretch your imagination quite wide, this may be the book for you. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6219198066249849974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2t0c1rZ59lD4Y4Sk+4DfN6retBKIfopHuKYTTDNGLtzNyAsRsrsI9iB70/cp59b41NY3BEs+yw4aL4FovFdu3A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mfM7jgXud0e8MXEcFsc2Lx1QRwMW3jIX9YMCaXb9RmKO5ixJASyJ4WQpJk/EoD/gY1jEFdWec15XCpBN+ewGYg==')})
  }

But when Ernest Bemis finds his wife, Cora, in a compromising situation with their neighbor, he doesn’t think of survival. In one impulsive moment, a man is dead, Ernest is off to prison, and the women left behind are divided by rage and remorse.\n\nLosing her husband to Cora’s indiscretion is another hardship for stoic Nettie Mae. But as a brutal Wyoming winter bears down, Cora and Nettie Mae have no choice but to come together as one family—to share the duties of working the land and raising their children. There’s Nettie Mae’s son, Clyde—no longer a boy, but not yet a man—who must navigate the road to adulthood without a father to guide him, and Cora’s daughter, Beulah, who is as wild and untamable as her prairie home.\n\nBound by the uncommon threads in their lives and the challenges that lie ahead, Cora and Nettie Mae begin to forge an unexpected sisterhood. But when a love blossoms between Clyde and Beulah, bonds are once again tested, and these two resilient women must finally decide whether they can learn to trust each other—or else risk losing
